            while(true)
            {
            try{
                char p=inputStr.charAt(count);
                int a=p;
                if(a>=65 && a<=90)
                {
                    changedString+=(char)(a+32);
                }
                else
                {
                    changedString+=p;
                }
                count++;
            }
            catch(StringIndexOutOfBoundsException e)
{
return changedString;
               }
            }
        }
        else
        {
            while(true)
            {
            try{
                char p=inputStr.charAt(count);
                int a=p;
                if(a>=97 && a<=122)
                {
                    changedString+=(char)(a-32);
                }
                else
                {
                    changedString+=p;
                }
                count++;
            }
            catch(StringIndexOutOfBoundsException e)
{
return changedString;
               }
            }
        }  
    }
    String findUniqueChars()
    {
        int count=0;
        String uni="";
        int a[]=new int[26];
        int as;
        int index;
        while(true)
        {
            try{
                char p=inputStr.charAt(count);
                as=p;
                if(as>=97 && as<=122)
                {
                    index=(as-97);
                    if(a[index]==0)
                    {
                        uni+=p;
                        a[index]=1;
                    }
                }
                if(as>=65 && as<=90)
                {
                    index=(as-65);
                    if(a[index]==0)
                    {
                        uni+=p;
                        a[index]=1;
                    }
                }
                count++;
            }
            catch(StringIndexOutOfBoundsException e)
{
return uni;
}
        }
    }
    boolean checkPalin()
    {
        int l=0;
        char [] s=inputStr.toCharArray();
        for(int i:s)
        {
           l++;
        }
        int count=0;
        while(true)
{
try{
                if(inputStr.charAt(count)!=inputStr.charAt(l-1-count))
                {
                    return false;
                }
                count++;
}
catch(StringIndexOutOfBoundsException e)
{
return true;
}
}
    }
}

25/02/23, 11:30â€¯am - .: #include<stdio.h>

int main()
{
	int a[5][9];
	for(int i=0;i<4;i++)
	{
		for(int j=0;j<8;j++)
		{
			scanf("%d",&a[i][j]);
		}
	}
	printf("\n");
	for(int i=0;i<4;i++)
	{
		for(int j=0;j<8;j++)
		{
			printf("%d ",a[i][j]);
		}
		printf("\n");
	}
	for(int i=0;i<4;i++)
	{
		int count = 0;
		for(int j=0;j<8;j++)
		{
			if(a[i][j]==1)count++;
		}
		count%2==0?(a[i][8]=0):(a[i][8]=1);

	}
	for(int i=0;i<9;i++)
	{
		int count = 0;
		for(int j=0;j<4;j++)
		{
			if(a[j][i]==1)count++;
		}
		count%2==0?(a[4][i]=0):(a[4][i]=1);
	}
	printf("\n");
	for(int i=0;i<5;i++)
	{
		for(int j=0;j<9;j++)
		{
			if(i==5)printf("\n");
			if(j==8)printf(" ");
			printf("%d ",a[i][j]);
		}
		printf("\n");
	}
}

30/05/23, 3:02â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: public class KeyFinder {
    public static int findKey(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int thousandsPlace = findLargestDigitInThousandsPlace(input1, input2, input3) -
                findSmallestDigitInThousandsPlace(input1, input2, input3);

        int hundredsPlace = findLargestDigitInHundredsPlace(input1, input2, input3) -
                findSmallestDigitInHundredsPlace(input1, input2, input3);

        int tensPlace = findLargestDigitInTensPlace(input1, input2, input3) -
                findSmallestDigitInTensPlace(input1, input2, input3);

        int unitsPlace = findLargestDigitInUnitsPlace(input1, input2, input3) -
                findSmallestDigitInUnitsPlace(input1, input2, input3);

        int key = (thousandsPlace * 1000) + (hundredsPlace * 100) + (tensPlace * 10) + unitsPlace;
        return key;
    }

    private static int findLargestDigitInThousandsPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int largestDigit = Math.max((input1 / 1000) % 10, Math.max((input2 / 1000) % 10, (input3 / 1000) % 10));
        return largestDigit;
    }

    private static int findSmallestDigitInThousandsPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int smallestDigit = Math.min((input1 / 1000) % 10, Math.min((input2 / 1000) % 10, (input3 / 1000) % 10));
        return smallestDigit;
    }

    private static int findLargestDigitInHundredsPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int largestDigit = Math.max((input1 / 100) % 10, Math.max((input2 / 100) % 10, (input3 / 100) % 10));
        return largestDigit;
    }

    private static int findSmallestDigitInHundredsPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int smallestDigit = Math.min((input1 / 100) % 10, Math.min((input2 / 100) % 10, (input3 / 100) % 10));
        return smallestDigit;
    }

    private static int findLargestDigitInTensPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int largestDigit = Math.max((input1 / 10) % 10, Math.max((input2 / 10) % 10, (input3 / 10) % 10));
        return largestDigit;
    }

    private static int findSmallestDigitInTensPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int smallestDigit = Math.min((input1 / 10) % 10, Math.min((input2 / 10) % 10, (input3 / 10) % 10));
        return smallestDigit;
    }

    private static int findLargestDigitInUnitsPlace(int input1, int input2, int input3) {
        int largestDigit = Math.max(input1 % 10, Math.max(input2 % 10, input3 % 10));
        return largestDigit;
    }

    private static int findSmallestDigitInUnitsPlace(int input1, int input

{

		int a[] = {10,41,18,50,43,29,31,25,59,96,67};
		int ans[]=new int[a.length];
		int indx=0;
		for(int i=0;i<a.length;i++)
		{
		    ans[i]=0;
		}
		for(int i=0;i<a.length;i++)
		{
		    int flag=0;
		    for(int j=2;j<=(a[i]/2);j++)
		    {
		        if(a[i]%j==0)
		        {
		            flag=1;
		            break;
		        }
		    }
		    if(flag==0)
		    {
		        //System.out.println(a[i]);

		    }
		}

	}
}

25/07/23, 11:48â€¯am - .: import java.util.*;
public class Main
{
    
    public static boolean prime(int n)
    {
        if(n==1)return false;
        for(int i=2;i<=(n/2);i++)
        {
            if(n%i==0)return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
    
	public static void main(String[] args) {
		Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
		int n = sc.nextInt();
		int ans = 0 ;
		while(n>0)
		{
		    int num = n%10;
		    if(prime(num))ans++;
		    n/=10;
		}
		System.out.println(ans);
	}
}

public class Main
{
	public static void main(String[] args) {
		Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
		String fn = sc.next();
		String ln = sc.next();
		int pin = sc.nextInt();
		int pos = sc.nextInt();
		String large,small;
		if(fn.length()==ln.length())
		{
		    String arr[] = new String[2];
		    arr[0] = fn;
		    arr[1] = ln;
		    Arrays.sort(arr,String.CASE_INSENSITIVE_ORDER);
    		 large = arr[1];
    		 small = arr[0];
		}
		else
		{
		    if(fn.length()<ln.length())
		    {
		         large = ln;
		         small = fn;
		    }
		    else
		    {
		         large = fn;
		         small = ln;
		    }
		}
		
		
// 		System.out.println(large);
// 		System.out.println(small);
		int temp = pin;
		String int_to_string = Integer.toString(pin);

		int l = int_to_string.length();
		int lp = int_to_string.charAt(pos-1) - '0';
		int rp = int_to_string.charAt(l-pos) - '0';
		String s = small.charAt(0)+large+(Integer.toString(lp))+(Integer.toString(rp));

		
		// toggle;
	    String s1 = "";
	    for (int i = 0; i < s.length(); i++) {
		    if(Character.isUpperCase(s.charAt(i))) 
			    s1=s1+Character.toLowerCase(s.charAt(i));
	    	 else 
			    s1=s1+Character.toUpperCase(s.charAt(i));
	    }
	    System.out.println(s1);
		
	}
}

{
	public static void main(String[] args) {
		int input1 = 3;
		String []input2 = new String[]{"Mango","Banana"};
		String ans="";
		for(String s : input2)
		{
		    String s1 = s.toLowerCase();
		    char f = s1.charAt(0);
		    char l = s1.charAt(s.length()-1);
		    if((f == 'a' || f == 'e' || f== 'i' || f == 'o' || f  == 'u' ) && (l == 'a' || l == 'e' || l== 'i' || l == 'o' || l  == 'u' ))
            {
                ans = ans+s1;
            }
		}
		if(ans.length()>0)
		    System.out.println(ans);
		else
		    System.out.println("no matches found");
	}
}

29/09/23, 2:26â€¯pm - .: public static void main(String[] args) {
		int input1 = 1274;
		int input2 = 5283;
		int input3 = 1937;
		int maxim = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
		int minim = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
		int a[] = new int[10];
		for(int i=0;i<10;i++)a[i]=0;
		while(input1>0)
		{
		    int num = input1%10;
		    input1/=10;
		    if(num>maxim)maxim=num;
		    if(num<minim)minim=num;
		    a[num]+=1;
		}
		while(input2>0)
		{
		    int num = input2%10;
		    input2/=10;
		    if(num>maxim)maxim=num;
		    if(num<minim)minim=num;
		    a[num]+=1;
		}
		while(input3>0)
		{
		    int num = input3%10;
		    input3/=10;
		    if(num>maxim)maxim=num;
		    if(num<minim)minim=num;
		    a[num]+=1;
		}
		int minf=0,maxf=0;
		for(int i=0;i<10;i++)
		{
		    if(a[i]!=0)
		    {
		        minf=i;
		        break;
		    }
		}
		for(int i=0;i<10;i++)
		{
		    if(a[i]==0)continue;
		    if(a[minf]>a[i])
		    {
		        minf=i;
		    }
		    if(a[maxf]<=a[i])
		    {
		        maxf=i;
		    }
		}
// 		System.out.println(maxim+" "+minim+" "+maxf+" "+minf);
		int ans  = ((1000*maxim) + (100*minim) + (10*maxf) + (minf));
		System.out.println(ans);
	
	}

public class MalwareAnalysis {
    public static int[] simulate(int[] entries) {
        int n = entries.length;

        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            if (entries[i] != 0) {
                int leftT = findLeftT(entries, i);
                int rightT = findRightT(entries, i);

                if (leftT >= entries[i] || rightT >= entries[i]) {
                    entries[i] = 0;
                }
            }
        }

        return entries;
    }

    private static int findLeftT(int[] entries, int index) {
        for (int i = index - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
            if (entries[i] != 0) {
                return entries[i];
            }
        }
        return 0; // If no 'T' is found on the left, consider it as 0.
    }

    private static int findRightT(int[] entries, int index) {
        int n = entries.length;
        for (int i = index + 1; i < n; i++) {
            if (entries[i] != 0) {
                return entries[i];
            }
        }
        return 0; // If no 'T' is found on the right, consider it as 0.
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] records = { 1, 2, 0, 5, 0, 2, 4, 3, 3, 3 };
        int[] result = simulate(records);

        System.out.println("The expected values after the malware runs are:");
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(result));
        // Expected output:
        // [1, 0, 0, 5, 0, 0, 0, 3, 3, 0]
    }
}

09/11/23, 6:53â€¯pm - .: import java.util.Arrays;

public class MalwareAnalysis {
    public static int[] simulate(int[] entries) {
      //throw new UnsupportedOperationException("Waiting to be implemented.");
      int s = entries.length;
      for(int i=0;i<s;i++)
      {
        int val = Math.max(entries[i],-1*entries[i]);
        int l = i-3;
        int r = i+4;
        if(l>=0)
        {
          int lv = Math.max(entries[l],-1*entries[l]);
          if(lv>=val)
          {
            entries[i] = -1*entries[i];
            continue;
          }
          
        }
        if(r<s)
        {
          int rv = Math.max(entries[r],-1*entries[r]);
          if(rv>=val)
          {
            entries[i] = entries[i]*-1;
            continue;
          }
        }
      }
      for(int i=0;i<s;i++)
      {
        if(entries[i]<0)entries[i] = 0;
      }
      return entries;
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] records = { 1, 2, 0, 5, 0, 2, 4, 3, 3, 3 };
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(simulate(records)));
        // Expected output:
        // 1, 0, 0, 5, 0, 0, 0, 3, 3, 0
    }
}

29/12/23, 2:41â€¯pm - .: chief.architect@ndmc.gov.in
29/12/23, 2:41â€¯pm - .: Subject : Urgent Appeal to Preserve Sunehri Masjid
29/12/23, 2:41â€¯pm - .: I am writing to express my deep concern regarding the recent proposal by the New Delhi Municipal Corporation (NDMC) to demolish the historic Sunehri Masjid, a monument that holds immense cultural and religious significance.

The Sunehri Masjid, standing for over a century, predates the establishment of New Delhi itself. Designated as a heritage building in 2009, this mosque is an integral part of our shared history and identity. Not only does it represent architectural brilliance, but it also served as the residence of Maulana Hasrat Mohani, adding to its historical importance.

The proposed demolition, citing the need for a 'smooth flow of traffic,' raises serious questions about the preservation of our cultural heritage. The mosque has stood resiliently for more than 150 years, and its destruction would not only erase an important historical site but also infringe upon the religious rights of the Muslim community.

The authorities of the masjid have provided evidence that traffic remains unaffected, even during Friday prayers, challenging the necessity of such a drastic measure. It is crucial to consider alternative solutions that prioritize the preservation of our cultural heritage while addressing traffic concerns.

I urge you to reconsider the proposal to demolish the Sunehri Masjid and explore options that ensure the coexistence of our heritage and the city's development. This issue requires a united effort to protect the historical and religious rights of the Muslim community in India.

Thank you for your attention to this matter. I trust that you will make a decision that reflects the values of cultural preservation and religious harmony.

Thanking You, 

A Responsible Citizen of India.

11/01/24, 4:12â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: def count_combinations(pieces, magic_number):
    piece_count = {}
    
    # Count the occurrences of each piece
    for piece in pieces:
        piece_count[piece] = piece_count.get(piece, 0) + 1

    combinations = 0

    # Iterate through the set of pieces to find valid combinations
    for piece in set(pieces):
        complement = magic_number - piece

        if complement in piece_count and piece_count[complement] > 0:
            # Found a valid combination
            combinations += 1
            piece_count[complement] -= 1
            piece_count[piece] -= 1

    return combinations

def main():
    n, k = map(int, input().split())
    pieces = list(map(int, input().split()))

    result = count_combinations(pieces, k)
    print(result)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

11/01/24, 4:15â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: In the bustling city of Puzzleville, a young prodigy Zoey stumbled upon a mysterious challenge left by a renowned puzzle master. Determined to solve it, she attempted to solve it.

Her mission was to arrange the pieces in unique combinations that would sum up to a magic number provided by the puzzle master. No piece can be used more thig once in a combination To help her crack the puzzle and reveal the secret prize, find the numbers of unique combinations that are possible.

INPUT

The first line of input contains positive integers N, representing the number of pieces and K, representing the magic number, separated by a space.

The next line contains the N numbers of positive integers, All, that represent the pieces.

OUTPUT

Print the number of combinations that are possible.

CONSTRAINTS

2 <= N <= 10^5

2 <= K <= N

1 <= A[i] <= 10*9

Example Input

7 8      10 1 2 7 6 1 5 output 4

INNER JOIN SCHEDULE s ON p.ID = s.PROFESSOR_ID

GROUP BY p.NAME, c.NAME;

17/03/24, 11:33â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: class Solution {
    public int minMeetingRooms(int[][] intervals) {
        // sorting intervals in increasing order of start time 
        Arrays.sort(intervals, (t1, t2) -> {
            return Integer.compare(t1[0], t2[0]);
        });
        int max=Integer.MIN_VALUE;
        
        // adding min heap for meeting/ task completed first to appear on top 
        PriorityQueue<int[]> pq = new PriorityQueue<>((t1,t2) -> {
            return Integer.compare(t1[1], t2[1]);
        });
        
        // iterating over all the intervals 
        for (int i=0;i<intervals.length;i++) {
            if (!pq.isEmpty()) {
                // if one of the allocated meeting rooms are free then remove it 
                if (pq.peek()[1] <= intervals[i][0]) {
                    pq.remove();
                }
            }
            pq.add(intervals[i]);
           // find if new size of allocated meeting rooms > old size of allocated meeting rooms
            max= Math.max(max, pq.size());
        }
        
        return max;
        
    }
}
17/03/24, 11:34â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
#include <queue>
#include <algorithm>

using namespace std;

struct TaxRun {
    int start;
    int end;
};

bool compareTaxRuns(const TaxRun& a, const TaxRun& b) {
    return a.start < b.start; // Sort tax runs by their start time
}

int minMachinesRequired(const vector<TaxRun>& taxRuns) {
    if (taxRuns.empty()) {
        return 0; // No tax runs, no machines needed
    }

    int numMachines = 1;  // Initialize with at least one machine
    priority_queue<int, vector<int>, greater<int>> endingTimes;  // Min heap for ending times
    vector<TaxRun> sortedRuns = taxRuns;  // Copy for sorting
    sort(sortedRuns.begin(), sortedRuns.end(), compareTaxRuns);

    endingTimes.push(sortedRuns[0].end);  // Add first tax run's end time to heap

    for (int i = 1; i < sortedRuns.size(); ++i) {
        int currentStart = sortedRuns[i].start;
        int earliestEndingTime = endingTimes.top();

        // If a machine is available (ending time is before current start), reuse it
        if (currentStart >= earliestEndingTime) {
            endingTimes.pop();  // Remove completed task from min heap
        } else {
            // Need a new machine as no available machine can handle the current task
            numMachines++;
        }

        // Add current tax run's end time to the heap
        endingTimes.push(sortedRuns[i].end);
    }

    return numMachines;
}

int main() {
    vector<TaxRun> taxRuns = {
        {1, 4}, {3, 5}, {0, 6}, {5, 7}, {3, 8}, {10, 12}, {11, 16}, {12, 14}
    };

    int minMachines = minMachinesRequired(taxRuns);
    cout << "Minimum number of machines required: " << minMachines << endl;

    return 0;
}
17/03/24, 11:42â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: #include <iostream>
#include <queue>
#include <vector>

using namespace std;

int find_min_machines(const vector<int>& start, const vector<int>& end) {
  """
  Finds the minimum number of machines required to complete a set of tasks.

  Args:
      start: A vector of start times for each task.
      end: A vector of end times for each task.

  Returns:
      The minimum number of machines required.
  """
  int n = start.size();
  vector<pair<int, int>> tasks;  // Stores task pairs (start, end)
  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
    tasks.push_back({start[i], end[i]});
  }

  sort(tasks.begin(), tasks.end());

  priority_queue<int, vector<int>, greater<int>> pq;  // Min-heap to store ongoing task end times
  int max_machines = 0;

  for (auto& task : tasks) {
    int task_start = task.first;
    int task_end = task.second;

    // Release machines that have finished tasks before the current one starts
    while (!pq.empty() && pq.top() <= task_start) {
      pq.pop();
    }

    // Add the ending time of the new task to the priority queue
    pq.push(task_end);
    // Update the maximum number of machines needed based on the size of the priority queue
    max_machines = max(max_machines, (int)pq.size());
  }

  return max_machines;
}

int main() {
  vector<int> start = {1, 8, 3, 9, 6};
  vector<int> end = {7, 9, 6, 14, 7};

  int min_machines = find_min_machines(start, end);
  cout << "Minimum number of machines required: " << min_machines << endl;

  return 0;
}

#include <queue>
#include <vector>

using namespace std;

int find_min_machines(const vector<int>& start, const vector<int>& end) {
  """
  Finds the minimum number of machines required to complete a set of tasks.

  Args:
      start: A vector of start times for each task.
      end: A vector of end times for each task.

  Returns:
      The minimum number of machines required.
  """
  int n = start.size();
  vector<pair<int, int>> tasks;  // Stores task pairs (start, end)
  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
    tasks.push_back({start[i], end[i]});
  }

  sort(tasks.begin(), tasks.end());

  priority_queue<int, vector<int>, greater<int>> pq;  // Min-heap to store ongoing task end times
  int max_machines = 0;

  for (auto& task : tasks) {
    int task_start = task.first;
    int task_end = task.second;

    // Release machines that have finished tasks before OR at the same time as the current one starts
    while (!pq.empty() && pq.top() <= task_start) {
      pq.pop();
    }

    // Add the ending time of the new task to the priority queue
    pq.push(task_end);
    // Update the maximum number of machines needed based on the size of the priority queue
    max_machines = max(max_machines, (int)pq.size());
  }

  return max_machines;
}

int main() {
  vector<int> start = {1, 8, 3, 9, 6};
  vector<int> end = {7, 9, 6, 14, 7};

  int min_machines = find_min_machines(start, end);
  cout << "Minimum number of machines required: " << min_machines << endl;

  return 0;
}
18/03/24, 12:12â€¯am - Saifullah RCCiit: Right ans
18/03/24, 12:12â€¯am - Saifullah RCCiit: import heapq

def find_min_machines(start, end):
    """
    Finds the minimum number of machines required to complete a set of tasks.

    Args:
        start: A list of start times for each task.
        end: A list of end times for each task.

    Returns:
        The minimum number of machines required.
    """
    n = len(start)
    tasks = sorted(zip(start, end), key=lambda x: x[0])  # Sort tasks based on start times

    pq = []  # Min-heap to store ongoing task end times
    max_machines = 0

    for task_start, task_end in tasks:
        # Release machines that have finished tasks before the current one starts
        while pq and pq[0] < task_start:
            heapq.heappop(pq)

        # Add the ending time of the new task to the priority queue
        heapq.heappush(pq, task_end)

        # Update the maximum number of machines needed based on the size of the priority queue
        max_machines = max(max_machines, len(pq))

    return max_machines

if __name__ == "__main__":
    start = [1, 8, 3, 9, 6]
    end = [7, 9, 6, 14, 7]

    min_machines = find_min_machines(start, end)
    print("Minimum number of machines required:", min_machines)

  s.first_name,
  s.last_name,
  s.email,
  SUM(CASE WHEN MONTH(d.deal_date) = 6 AND YEAR(d.deal_date) = 2022 THEN d.deal_amount ELSE 0 END) AS total

21/03/24, 11:51â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: def min_moves_to_delete(word):
  """
  Finds the minimum number of moves needed to get a word of minimal length.

  Args:
      word: A string containing lowercase English letters.

  Returns:
      The minimum number of moves required.
  """

  n = len(word)
  dp = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]  # dp[i][j]: minimum moves to reduce word[i:j+1] to a single character

  # Base cases: single characters or adjacent duplicates
  for i in range(n):
    dp[i][i] = 0
    if i + 1 < n and word[i] == word[i + 1]:
      dp[i][i + 1] = 1

  # Build up the DP table
  for length in range(2, n):  # length of substring
    for i in range(n - length + 1):  # starting index of substring
      j = i + length - 1  # ending index of substring
      min_moves = float('inf')
      isolated = False  # Flag to track isolated character within substring

      for k in range(i, j + 1):  # try deleting character at each index
        if word[k] == word[i] or word[k] == word[j]:  # character matches either end
          cost = dp[i][k - 1] + (dp[k + 1][j] if k + 1 <= j else 0)
          min_moves = min(min_moves, cost)
        else:
          # character doesn't match either end, consider isolation
          isolated = True
      # If no deletions within the substring but a character is isolated, count 1 move
      if not isolated:
        min_moves = min(min_moves, 1)
      dp[i][j] = min_moves

  return dp[0][n - 1]

# Example usage
word = "baabacaa"
min_moves = min_moves_to_delete(word)
print(min_moves)  # Output: 3

22/03/24, 12:31â€¯am - Saifullah RCCiit: vowels = set('aeiouAEIOU')
consonants = set('bcdfghjklmnpqrstvwxyzBCDFGHJKLMNPQRSTVWXYZ')
alphanum = set('0123456789' + ''.join(vowels | consonants))

def count_valid_words(s):
  """
  Counts the number of valid words in a string.

  Args:
      s: A string containing alphanumeric characters.

  Returns:
      The number of valid words in the string.
  """
  count = 0
  word_start = 0
  has_vowel = False
  has_consonant = False

  for i, char in enumerate(s):
    if char not in alphanum:
      # Invalid character, reset word
      word_start = i + 1
      has_vowel = False
      has_consonant = False
    elif char in vowels:
      has_vowel = True
    elif char in consonants:
      has_consonant = True
    else:
      # Handle numbers
      pass

    if i - word_start >= 2 and has_vowel and has_consonant:
      count += 1
      word_start = i + 1
      has_vowel = False
      has_consonant = False

  return count

# Example usage
s = "leetcode"
valid_words = count_valid_words(s)
print(f"Number of valid words in '{s}': {valid_words}")

25/04/24, 7:42â€¯pm - .: #include <bits/stdc++.h>
using namespace std;

string prefix(string a, string b)
{
    string ans = "";
    for(int i=0;i<(min(a.size(),b.size()));++i)
    {
        if(a[i]==b[i])ans+=a[i];
        else break;
    }
    return ans;
}

int main()
{
    vector<string> v = {"tcsdigital","tcsninja","tcsprime"};
    
    string ans = v[0];
    
    for(int i=1;i<v.size();++i)
    {
        ans = prefix(ans,v[i]);
    }
    cout<<ans;

    return 0;
}

02/06/24, 5:45â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: ### Detailed Responses from the Candidate

1. **Where is the `synchronized` keyword used?**

   The `synchronized` keyword in Java is used to control access to a block of code or a method by multiple threads. It ensures that only one thread can execute the synchronized block or method at a time, thus preventing race conditions and ensuring thread safety. There are two main ways to use the `synchronized` keyword:

   - **Synchronized Method**: The entire method is synchronized, and the lock is held on the object instance (or the class if the method is static).

     ```java
     public synchronized void synchronizedMethod() {
         // synchronized code
     }
     ```

   - **Synchronized Block**: A specific block of code within a method is synchronized, and the lock is held on a specified object.

     ```java
     public void method() {
         synchronized(this) {
             // synchronized code
         }
     }
     ```

   Using `synchronized` ensures that critical sections of code are executed by only one thread at a time, preventing data inconsistency and ensuring correct program behavior in a multi-threaded environment.

2. **What are tuples in Python?**

   Tuples in Python are immutable sequences, typically used to store collections of heterogeneous data. Once a tuple is created, its elements cannot be changed, which makes tuples a type-safe and hashable data structure. This immutability also means that tuples can be used as keys in dictionaries, unlike lists which are mutable.

   - **Creating a Tuple**:
     ```python
     my_tuple = (1, 2, 3)
     another_tuple = ("a", "b", "c")
     ```
   
   - **Accessing Elements**:
     ```python
     first_element = my_tuple[0]  # 1
     ```

   - **Advantages**:
     - **Performance**: Tuples are generally faster than lists.
     - **Immutability**: Provides data integrity since the data cannot be changed accidentally.
     - **Hashable**: Can be used as dictionary keys.

3. **Why do we use SQL?**

   SQL (Structured Query Language) is used for managing and manipulating relational databases. It is the standard language for interacting with databases and is used to perform various operations such as:

   - **Data Querying**: Extracting data using `SELECT` statements.
   - **Data Insertion**: Adding new data using `INSERT` statements.
   - **Data Updating**: Modifying existing data using `UPDATE` statements.
   - **Data Deletion**: Removing data using `DELETE` statements.
   - **Database Management**: Creating and modifying database schema using `CREATE`, `ALTER`, and `DROP` statements.
   - **Data Control**: Managing access to the database using `GRANT` and `REVOKE` statements.

   SQL provides a powerful and flexible way to interact with databases, enabling efficient storage, retrieval, and manipulation of data.

4. **Commands in Git**

   Git is a version control system used to track changes in source code during software development. Some commonly used Git commands include:

   - **Initialization**:
     ```bash
     git init
     ```

   - **Cloning a Repository**:
     ```bash
     git clone <repository_url>
     ```

   - **Checking Status**:
     ```bash
     git status
     ```

   - **Adding Changes**:
     ```bash
     git add <file_or_directory>
     git add .
     ```

   - **Committing Changes**:
     ```bash
     git commit -m "Commit message"
     ```

   - **Pushing to Remote Repository**:
     ```bash
     git push origin <branch_name>
     ```

   - **Pulling from Remote Repository**:
     ```bash
     git pull
     ```

   - **Creating a New Branch**:
     ```bash
     git branch <branch_name>
     ```

   - **Switching Branches**:
     ```bash
     git checkout <branch_name>
     ```

   - **Merging Branches**:
     ```bash
     git merge <branch_name>
     ```

   - **Viewing Commit History**:
     ```bash
     git log
     ```

5. **Questions on Project (Video Demo)**

   - **Course Management System**:
     - Can you demonstrate the user interface and walk us through the process of adding, updating, and deleting a course?
     - How did you handle user authentication and authorization in the system?
     - Could you show how the RESTful APIs interact with the frontend and backend?

   - **Airline Fair Prediction**:
     - Can you show the steps of data preprocessing and how the model makes predictions?
     - How do you evaluate the performance of the machine learning model, and what metrics do you use?
     - Could you demonstrate the user interface of the prediction website and walk us through the prediction process?

6. **B-Tree and B+ Tree**

   - **B-Tree**:
     - B-Tree is a self-balancing tree data structure that maintains sorted data and allows for efficient insertion, deletion, and search operations.
     - Each node in a B-Tree contains multiple keys and children pointers, and all leaf nodes are at the same level.
     - B-Trees are commonly used in databases and file systems to manage large amounts of data due to their ability to minimize disk I/O operations.

   - **B+ Tree**:
     - B+ Tree is an extension of B-Tree where all values are stored at the leaf level, and internal nodes only store keys and act as a guide to the leaves.
     - Leaf nodes are linked together to form a linked list, allowing for efficient range queries.
     - B+ Trees provide better performance for range queries and are widely used in database indexing and file systems.

   **Comparison**:
   - **Structure**:
     - B-Tree: Keys and data are stored in all nodes.
     - B+ Tree: Keys are stored in internal nodes; data is stored only in leaf nodes.

   - **Efficiency**:
     - B-Tree: Suitable for exact match queries.
     - B+ Tree: More efficient for range queries due to linked leaf nodes.

   These structures ensure that data remains balanced and accessible in logarithmic time, which is crucial for large-scale data storage and retrieval systems.

    long ans = 0;
    for(int i=0;i<l;i++)
    {
        for(int j=i+1;j<l;j++)
        {
            ans += abs(s[i]-s[j]);
        }
    }
    return ans;

07/07/24, 12:39â€¯pm - Saifullah RCCiit: def lcm(a, b):
    return abs(a * b) // math.gcd(a, b)

# Function to calculate the LCM of a list of numbers
def lcm_multiple(numbers):
    return reduce(lcm, numbers, 1)

# Function to count the subsets whose LCM is divisible by k
def count_subsets(arr, k):
    n = len(arr)
    count = 0
    
    # Iterate through all possible non-empty subsets
    for i in range(1, n + 1):
        for subset in combinations(arr, i):
            if lcm_multiple(subset) % k == 0:
                count += 1
                
    return count
